#_x000D_

Government Business Architecture Reference Model Version 5.0
ABOUT THE BUSINESS ARCHITECTURE CONTENTS HEREIN

The business architecture reference model contained herein represents a basic business architecture for a
generic government at multiple levels of jurisdiction. This version of the government reference model incl
a capability map, value streams common to most governments, an information map, organization map, an
stakeholder map. This reference model is a work-in-progress and will continue to evolve based on Guild
member contributions.
USAGE and DISCLAIMERS
Business Architecture Guild® represents that the business architecture content contained herein:
• IS DELIVERED AS-IS WITH NO CLAIM OF WARRANTY
• Is to be used at one’s own risk
• May be modified or augmented for use at one’s own discretion
• Is not intended to fully represent a complete business architecture perspective
• Does not represent any specific tool import or export format
• May be updated by the Guild at any point in time to reflect evolution of the practice
• Is not presented as being free from errors or omissions
• IS FOR INTERNAL USE ONLY AND NOT FOR DISTRIBUTION TO 3RD PARTIES
Comments should be directed to the appropriate Business Architecture Guild reference model member forum at
www.businessarchitectureguild.org.

Guild member forum.

Capability Map

Definition
Ability to establish, organize, analyze, administer, and report on all aspects of a name, symbol, or design that identifies and differentiates
products, offerings, or organizational identities.
Ability to establish and identify a brand.
Ability to declare a brand.
Ability to recognize a brand.
Ability to organize, aggregate, segment, and prioritize a collection of brands.
Ability to determine how well a brand is meeting specification and objective levels, or delivering against plan.
Ability to determine acceptable or unacceptable levels of performance for a brand.
Ability to determine if a brand is exceeding or falling short of an acceptable threshold of performance.
Ability to assess what is causing a brand to underperform.
Ability to assess and quantify the commitment and staying power that the brand has within the markets in which it has a presence.
Ability to assess and quantify the degree of familiarity and recognition a brand has within and across various markets.
Ability to identify and specify the stakeholders, markets, locations, and industry sectors marked for building brand awareness.
Ability to identify, assess, aggregate, articulate, and incorporate various exposures to harm, danger, or loss associated with a brand.
Ability to identify and define the level of risk associated with a brand.
Ability to identify and define the level of acceptable risk associated with a brand.
Ability to consider a collective set of risk factors about a brand and represent them from a rationalized perspective.
Ability to define, interpret, and enforce the right to view, use, or modify a brand or its component parts.
Ability to determine access rights limitations for a brand.
Ability to understand the access rights limitations for a brand.
Ability to impose access rights limitations for a brand.
Ability to associate a brand with other business objects.
Ability to associate a brand with a channel.
Ability to associate a brand with an intellectual property right.
Ability to associate a brand with an infrastructure.
Ability to associate a brand with a message.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Ability to associate a brand with a partner.
Ability to associate a brand with a plan.
Ability to associate a brand with a policy.
Ability to associate a brand with a public sector entity.
Ability to associate a brand with a strategy.
Ability to collect, organize, monitor, report on, and otherwise disseminate basic facts, statistics, attributes, and data about a brand.
Ability to articulate, organize, identify, track, validate, and otherwise administer descriptive, identifying information about a brand and their
relationships.
Ability to determine, modify, and interpret the category or classification of a brand.
Ability to determine, modify, and interpret the status or condition of a brand.
Ability to identify, record, and represent a chronological order of events and actions associated with a brand.
Ability to identify, establish, validate, and articulate metrics and measures on historic and predictive determinations of a brand.
Ability to identify the need for, plan, design, execute, and measure the effectiveness of an outreach activity that targets a specific
population, for example, constituents, human resources, partners, or patients, to achieve a certain goal such as marketing awareness,
hiring activities, and health awareness.
Ability to establish and identify a campaign.
Ability to declare a campaign.
Ability to recognize a campaign.
Ability to define campaign collateral, including target-specific messaging, graphic designs for each delivery channel, as well as identify the
right channel mix and execution sequence.
Ability to capture a campaign target's interests, actions, and answers.
Ability to define and optimize the campaign spend versus the value being delivered.
Ability to project the value being delivered through a campaign.
Ability to project the required spend to deliver a campaign.
Ability to balance the spend versus value-add for a campaign.
Ability to organize, aggregate, segment, and prioritize a collection of campaigns.
Ability to classify and analyze campaigns based on specific attributes.
Ability to group campaigns.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Ability to evaluate and prioritize a collection of campaigns within a portfolio, based on specific attributes, such as cost, benefit, target
demographic, and channel.
Ability to determine how well a campaign is meeting specification and objective levels, or delivering against plan.
Ability to determine acceptable or unacceptable levels of performance for a campaign.
Ability to determine if a campaign is exceeding or falling short of an acceptable threshold of performance.
Ability to assess what is causing a campaign to underperform.
Ability to identify, assess, aggregate, articulate, and incorporate various exposures to harm, danger, or loss associated with a campaign.
Ability to identify and define the level of risk associated with a campaign.
Ability to identify and define the level of acceptable risk associated with a campaign.
Ability to consider a collective set of risk factors about a campaign and represent them from a rationalized perspective.
Ability to define, interpret, and enforce the right to view, use, or modify a campaign or its component parts.
Ability to determine access rights limitations for a campaign.
Ability to understand the access rights limitations for a campaign.
Ability to impose access rights limitations for a campaign.
Ability to associate a campaign with other business objects.
Ability to associate a campaign with a brand.
Ability to associate a campaign with a channel.
Ability to associate a campaign with a constituent.
Ability to associate a campaign with energy.
Ability to associate a campaign with content.
Ability to associate a campaign with a financial forecast.
Ability to associate a campaign with a financial position.
Ability to associate a campaign with a government service.
Ability to associate a campaign with an initiative.
Ability to associate a campaign with an intellectual property right.
Ability to associate a campaign with a job.
Ability to associate a campaign with a location.
Ability to associate a campaign with a market.
Ability to associate a campaign with a natural resource.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

Ability to associate a campaign with a partner.

Value Stream Inventory
Value Stream Definition/Description

The end-to-end perspective of acquiring an asset, from initiating and approving the asset request, to sourcing and
processing procurement orders and delivering the asset to the requester.
The end-to-end perspective of obtaining coverage to indemnify against loss.

The end-to-end perspective of applying for, qualifying for, and receiving a new or renewal of a license or permit.
The end-to-end perspective of determining the degree to which the organization is adhering to established policies
and regulations.
The end-to-end perspective of determining the degree to which the individual or organization is adhering to
established policies and regulations, such as for financial, tax, or election violation probes.
The end-to-end perspective of setting scope, determining study means, designing the study, gathering research,
producing findings, and delivering recommendations.
The end-to-end perspective of planning and executing the means, typically by ballot, to establish the constituents'
choice for, or re-call of, a particular candidate(s), proposition, plebiscite, or referendum question.
The end-to-end perspective involved in the creation or update of policies that govern how the public sector entity will
regulate constituent organizations, including the operations of the public sector entity itself.
The end-to-end perspective of crossing or sending something across a geographic border.
The end-to-end perspective of bringing a case, evidence, and testimony through the court system, obtaining a
decision, and enacting the decision.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

The end-to-end perspective of planning and executing an initiative.

The end-to-end perspective of planning and executing a meeting.

The end-to-end perspective of planning, executing, and communicating a training course for the purpose of increasing
knowledge and skill.
The end-to-end perspective of making an asset available for use within the organization and to the individual(s)
requesting the asset.
The end-to-end perspective involved in creating and launching a new or modifying or decommissioning an existing
government service.
The end-to-end perspective of planning, specifying, designing, and commissioning major or minor modifications to
infrastructure, including roads, railways, bridges, tunnels, stations, rail corridors, and related structures.
The end-to-end perspective of developing an individual's career, from performance assessment to skills and
experience enhancement and individual redeployment.
The end-to-end perspective of developing or refining a set of integrated and aligned visions, goals, objectives, and
courses of action that provide direction and guides activity.
The end-to-end perspective of requesting, creating, and delivering of information products to requester.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

The end-to-end perspective of ensuring conformance with legislation and organization-driven policies, from identifying
compliance requirements, implementing controls, evaluating controls' effectiveness, addressing compliance incidents,
and reporting compliance as required.
The end-to-end perspective of activities necessary for establishing a new or updating an existing agreement with a
partner or a constituent.
The end-to-end perspective of designing, articulating, approving, updating, and publishing a standard.

The end-to-end perspective of executing a campaign, from identifying the need for a campaign, to planning, designing,
implementing, and measuring the effectiveness of the campaign.
The end-to-end perspective involved in completing a financial transaction for an agreement.
The end-to-end perspective of planning, initiating, running, and terminating an operation.
The end-to-end value delivery perspective for creating a ready-to-acquire product.
The end-to-end perspective of applying for, qualifying for, and receiving a new or renewal of a certification.

The end-to-end perspective of a government organization receiving a request for, approving, and providing financial
assistance.
The end-to-end perspective of submitting a request, being qualified for, and receiving the requested service.

The end-to-end perspective of establishing the right to own, use, and develop government-owned, community-owned,
or privately-owned land.
The end-to-end perspective of identifying, exploring, and selecting an individual to fill a need within an organization.

#_x000D_

The end-to-end perspective of identifying and commencing business with other organizations for mutual benefit.
The end-to-end perspective of deciding where to make investments, based on the understanding of the enterprise's

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

I

Information Concept

Information
Concept Category

Accreditation

Primary

An endorsement by a duly recognized and acknowledged third
party that indicates ability, competence, knowledge, provenance,
or quality.

Agreement

Primary

A set of legally binding rights and obligations between two or
more legal entities.

Agreement Term

Secondary

A legally enforceable condition set forth within the bounds of an
agreement.

Asset

Primary

Tangible or intangible property.

Biological Organism

Primary

Non-human living thing.

Brand

Primary

A name, symbol, or design that identifies and differentiates
products, offerings, or organizational identities.

Campaign

Primary

An outreach activity that targets a specific population, for
example, constituents, human resources, partners, and patients,
to achieve a certain goal, such as marketing awareness, hiring
activities, and health awareness.

Case

Primary

An instance of a need or demand that requires resolution, such
as in the context of legal, social welfare, healthcare, or related
government services.

Channel

Primary

A digital, analog, or physical conduit through which products,
related services, or communications are delivered or received,
including the Internet, phone, delivery service, satellite, radio, or
physical means.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Claim

Primary

A demand or request to indemnify constituents under the terms
of an agreement.

Competency

Primary

The skills and knowledge necessary to do something.

Constituent

Primary

An individual or entity relative to an organization's sphere of
responsibility.

Content

Primary

A creative work or other authored item, such as is manifested in
audio/visual, still image, textual, experiential, mixed-media, or
other forms.

Content Impression

Secondary

An instance of content consumption.

Conveyor

Primary

An apparatus or assembly, whether human or robot-piloted, that
has the capacity to transport people and physical items, such as
animals, goods, or other assets.

Decision

Primary

A conclusion or resolution reached after considering alternative
options.

Dispute

Primary

An argument, disagreement, or protest of perceived injustice.

Energy

Primary

Sources of power.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Event

Primary

An occurrence that has happened or may happen, especially one
of importance, concern, or interest.

Evidence

Primary

Proof to support a proposition.

Finance

Primary

Monetary aspects and resources.

Currency

Secondary

An agreed medium of value exchange.

Financial Account

Secondary

A named container of monetary value transactions that are
typically organized into assets, liabilities, income, expense, equity,
and other related categories.

Financial Forecast

Secondary

A financial estimate, prediction, or projection.

Financial Position

Secondary

A consolidated and holistic representation of actual financial
standing or activity for a point in time or duration.

Financial Transaction

Secondary

An instance of a monetary amount movement or related
exchange across businesses, agreements, or financial accounts.

Monetary Amount

Secondary

A representation of value as expressed in a given currency.

Payment

Secondary

An obligation to remit or receive a monetary amount between an
organization and a constituent, partner, or other external party.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Tax

Secondary

A compulsory contribution of monetary value to governing
bodies.

Financial Instrument

Primary

A tradeable asset, such as stocks, bonds, bills of exchange,
futures, options, evidence of ownership, and cash.

Geographic Space

Primary

A physical area across land, air, and water.

Geographic Border

Secondary

A line of demarcation around a geographic space or between one
geographic space and another geographic space.

Government Service

Primary

A named combination of goods, doing-of-work-for-others, and
entitlements that can be offered to constituents.

Health Condition

Primary

A state of well-being of a human being or biological organism.

Human Resource

Primary

An individual who has, plans to have, or has had a legal
agreement with the organization, which may include
compensation and other benefits, on a temporary or permanent
basis.

Incident

Primary

An unplanned, disruptive or potentially disruptive experience.

Infrastructure

Primary

A physical structure or facility, which may include power grids,
communication lines, railways, roadways, bridges, tunnels, and
pipelines or conduits for water, gas, and power.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Initiative

Primary

A coordinated collection of temporary endeavors undertaken to
create a unique outcome.

Inquiry

Primary

A question, request, feedback, or comment that may exist inside
or outside of the organization.

Intellectual Property Rights Primary

A legal protection, such as patent, trademark, or copyright.

Interaction

Primary

Investment Portfolio

Primary

A set of contemporaneous collaborations or contacts about a
given subject, over a span of time, between two or more entities,
using one or more channels, at one or more physical or virtual
locations such as meetings, interviews, seminars, or
consultations.
A set of resources expected to increase in value or provide
income.

Job

Primary

A named category of accountabilities, whether remunerative or
non-remunerative, associated with an assigned, specific, and
accountable business duty, role, or function that can be executed
by a human or non-human resource.

Language

Primary

A method of communication or dialect variant consisting of units
of representation or meaning, such as numbers, words, symbols,
sounds, or other physical manifestations and gestures, presented
in a structured way.

Legislation

Primary

A set of authoritative directives that include laws or related
statutory instruments.

License

Primary

An authorization to perform a regulated activity, awarded by duly
recognized governmental agency or third party, applied to an
individual or organization, to engage in an activity, such as
fishing, or use of regulated objects, such as modes of
transportation or hazardous materials.

License Term

Secondary

A legally enforceable condition set forth within the bounds of a
license.

Location

Primary

A position or site.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Market

Primary

Individuals, populations of individuals, or organizations
constituting the demand for existing or future products and
services.

Material

Primary

Food, ingredients, chemicals, waste, and other physical elements
used to enable an outcome including sustaining life, the growing
of crops, the construction of assets and infrastructure, and the
powering of equipment and conveyors.

Message

Primary

A verbal, written, recorded, or digitally-represented
communication, including missives, notifications, alerts, and
other internally or externally targeted communication about the
organization's mission, products, plans, activities, and other focal
points.

Natural Resource

Primary

Matter that can occur in nature.

Network

Primary

A set of connected arcs and nodes that may be associated with
infrastructure, assets, locations, routes, and other business
objects.

Network Arc

Secondary

A connection or association between nodes in a network.

Network Node

Secondary

A connection point in a network.

Operation

Primary

An orchestration of work to achieve a specific objective
constrained by time and location, which may include, for
example, transportation center, monitoring station, law
enforcement, or administrative shift cycles across government.

Order

Primary

An instruction, by one party to another, to buy, sell, exchange,
provide, or deliver goods or services.

Order Item

Secondary

An order element that refers to a specific good or service.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Partner

Primary

A legal entity that has, plans to have, or has had some degree of
involvement with the organization.

Plan

Primary

An organized, sequenced set of steps or instructions, which may
include milestones, intended to achieve a result when completed.

Policy

Primary

A set of rules, procedures, regulations, and principles, or, a
codified proposed intent.

Public Sector Entity

Primary

A governmental body or collection of governmental bodies.

Research

Primary

A systematic investigation into materials and sources intended to
establish facts and produce insights.

Route

Primary

A way or course taken in getting from a starting point to a
destination, which may include stops along the way.

Schedule

Primary

An aggregation of schedule elements.

Schedule Element

Secondary

A line item that aligns time and one or more other objects,
including work item, human resource, payment, event, or
location.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Standard

Primary

A convention, specification, or measurement, confirmed by a
recognized governance body.

Strategy

Primary

An integrated and aligned association of visions, goals,
objectives, and courses of action that provides direction and
guides activity.

Course of Action

Secondary

A set of activities to be taken to achieve an objective.

Goal

Secondary

An end toward which effort is or should be directed.

Objective

Secondary

A quantitative, measurable result that contributes to the
realization of a goal.

Vision

Secondary

An imagined future state of being.

Submission

Primary

A container that is used to exchange one or more requests,
inquiries, messages, notifications, content, or other objects
between parties.

Time

Primary

A point or duration in the past, present, or future.

Training Course

Primary

A structured theoretical or practical subject matter in a
consumable format, associated with a curriculum, workshop, or
seminar.

Trip

Primary

A journey between a starting point location and one or more
targeted locations until a final destination is reached.

Vote

Primary

A formal indication of choice such as for a candidate election,
referendum, or proposition.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Work

Primary

Tasks and task queues.

Work Item

Secondary

A defined, well-bounded task that may be assigned to a
stakeholder or corresponding asset.

Work Queue

Secondary

A container to hold, sequence, filter, structure, and present a set
of work items.

Information Concept: The information concept realizes or makes explicit a business object, which would be derived from the capability

Information Concept Category: Primary information concept realizes a business object that is not dependent on another business objec
information concept. A secondary information concept realizes a business object that is fully dependent on another business object for
object.
Information Concept Definition: The definition of an information concept is derived from the object portion of the capability definition

Information Concept Type: Type represents the different variations of the information concept and can be multidimensional. For examp

Related Information Concepts: Relationships among information concepts reflect real world relationships among business objects. A re
Information Concept States: A list of possible information concept statuses or conditions.

Business Unit

Business Unit Level: Level begins at level 0 for the enterprise and decomposes from there.
Business Unit: Name of the business unit being mapped.
Business Unit Type: Categories include Enterprise (top level), Business Unit, Partner (external entities), and Collaborative Team.
Description: A summary of the overall role of this business unit.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Capabilities: List of capabilities a business unit possesses and can enact.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Organization Map
Definition
A national government, possibly comprised of the legislative, executive, and judicial bodies, running a
nation on behalf of its constituents.
Responsible for establishing and updating the laws of the nation.
Lower chamber of the bicameral legislative body, responsible for the development, evaluation, and
enactment of national legislation.
Upper chamber of the bicameral legislative body, responsible for the development, evaluation, and
enactment of national legislation.
Provides auditing, evaluation, and investigative services for the national legislative body.
Responsible for the production and distribution of information products and services for all branches of the
national government.
Provides central library, research, and archival services to the nation.
Responsible for the provision of independent analysis to support the budgetary and economic processes of
the national legislative body.
Responsible for providing support to the executive body of the government, which includes the executive of
the nation, e.g., a prime minister or president. Business units are responsible for communications, media
briefings, and budget management.
Oversees the direction of staff and advisors, ensuring effective and efficient support to the organization's
senior leadership.
Provides analysis and advice on domestic and international economic policy to support the national
executive.
Provides reports and advice on environmental policy and issues to support the national executive.
Responsible for the coordination of policy on national security issues and provision of advice to the national
executive.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Provides administrative services to all entities of the National Executive Office, including direct support to
the incumbent holder of the Executive Office. Services can include financial management and information
technology support, human resources management, library and research assistance, facilities
management, procurement, printing and graphics support, security, and mail and messenger services.
Provides organizational leadership on strategic, operational, and administrative matters, which can include
the domains of budget, financial management, risk management, initiative and resource management,
human capital management, asset management, and executive secretariat.
Manages the orchestration of policy development, internal and/or external, delivery and policy-focused
advice to the organization and its leadership in executing its remit. Policy development is often domainfocused, e.g., health policy, veterans services policy, defense policy, tax policy.
Responsible for policy and provision of advice to the national executive office on scientific, engineering, and
technological matters relating to the national economy, national security, homeland security, health,
foreign relations, the environment, and the technological use of resources.
Responsible for policy and advice to the national executive on issues relating to trade policy. Responsible
for conducting bilateral and multilateral trade negotiations and the coordination of trade policy across the
national government.
Highest tribunal in the nation for all cases under the laws of the country.
The intermediate appellate courts of the national judiciary, responsible for being the final arbiter in most
appeal cases.
Responsible for acting as the main trial courts in the national judiciary for civil and criminal cases.
Responsible for acting as the main civil and criminal courts in territories falling under the control of the
national judiciary.
Responsible for overseeing cases pertaining to international trade and customs.
Responsible for adjudicating disputes concerning national taxation, such as income tax disputes.
Responsible for the support of the judicial branch through the provision of administrative, legal, financial,
management, program, and information technology services.
Responsible for leadership and policy to the nation on agriculture, food, natural resources, nutrition, and
rural development.
Responsible for the synchronization and co-ordination of strategic direction and policy across the
organization's administrations, offices, and officials.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Provides oversight of civil and constitutional rights of constituents through legislation, policies, and actions.
Oversees and coordinates communications and administrative processes between the organization and the
primary office of the legislative government.
Responsible for human resources, facilities, security and emergency planning, equal employment
opportunity, library services, executive secretariat, and administrative support function.
Responsible for independent oversight, conducting audits and investigations, providing policy
recommendations, and informing designated officials as to the status and deficiencies in the organization.
Advises the leadership and senior departmental officials regarding laws, regulations, executive orders, and
judicial precedent pertaining to the organization and its operations. Responsible for legal and litigation
services and support for legislative and regulatory activities.
Responsible for budget development and allocation, monitoring execution of funds to networks, and
oversees financial management and accounting operations.
Responsible for the provision of objective, robust, and high-quality analysis to inform the policy
development and decision-making processes.
Responsible for coordinating the preparation of organizational budget estimates, legislative reports, and
regulation.
Manages the organization's internal and external communication channels and is responsible for delivering
communication solutions that support the organization's strategic objectives.
Responsible for media briefings, handling press enquiries, and the development of communication
material.
Provides representation and coordination with community leaders and groups.
Oversees the appeals process and other legal challenges, such as judicial and administrative reviews to and
by the organization. Manages appeals for claims relating to constituents, staff, and government.
Enables the organization through the provision of efficient, effective, secure, and reliable technology
services.
Responsible for developing food safety education, training, and technical assistance resources to support
programs.
Oversees the marketing and promotion of the nation's agricultural products.

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Oversees programs developing and protecting the nation's natural and environmental resources in support
of agriculture.
Responsible for administrating the organization's nutrition and food security programs and the promotion
of dietary guidelines.
Responsible for overseeing risk mitigation initiatives, such as crop insurance services, conservation
programs, and technical assistance, and commodity, lending, and disaster programs.
Provides analysis and policy to connect the nation's agricultural products and services to the global network
and international trade.
Responsible for research, analysis, and education to develop safe, sustainable, and competitive food and
agricultural system.
Responsible for overseeing initiatives to develop the economy and quality of life in rural areas through
financial products, loans, grants, guarantees, and other services.
Promotes job creation, commerce, and economic growth by ensuring fair trade, the provision of supporting
data, setting of standards, and conducting research and development.
Responsible for the synchronization and co-ordination of strategic direction and policy across the
organization's administrations, offices, and officials.
Promotes sustainable economic development through investment policy targeted on innovation and
competitiveness.
Responsible for promoting the growth and competitiveness of minority-owned businesses through access
to capital, contracts, and market opportunities.
Responsible for the collection and organization of scientific, technical, engineering, and business
information generated by government-backed research and development.
Advises the national government on telecommunication policy and regulation.
Acts as the primary point of contact between the organization and the business community.
Responsible for budget development and allocation, monitoring execution of funds to networks, and
oversees financial management and accounting operations.
Enables the organization through the provision of efficient, effective, secure, and reliable technology
services.

Supports the organization's executive function, including secretary and ministerial, in fulfilling its remit and
achieving its aims and objectives.

judicial precedent pertaining to the organization and its operations. Responsible for legal and litigation
services and support for legislative and regulatory activities.

Responsible for the development of strategic policy priorities and the provision of policy advice to the

Manages the organization's internal and external communication channels and is responsible for delivering

Oversees and coordinates communications and administrative processes between the organization and the

Responsible for measuring and disseminating information about the nation’s dynamic economy, society,
and institutions, fostering economic growth, advancing scientific understanding, and facilitating informed
decisions.
Provides statistical and economic accounts data for the government to inform budget development,
monetary policy, planning, and investment.
Provides analysis and reporting on national economic and demographic data.
Responsible for the provision of objective, robust and high-quality analysis to inform the policy
development and decision-making processes.
Responsible for issues involving national security and technology through export regulation and controls.
Responsible for the development, implementation, and enforcement of export controls.
Responsible for administering laws relating to patents and trademarks.
Responsible for the administration of laws relating to patents and trademarks and the provision of advice
on intellectual property matters.

Provision of advice on exports and the enforcement of safeguards against unfair competition relating to

Promotion of the nation's trade through the provision of business matchmaking, market intelligence, trade

Responsible for national marine resources, conservation, and management of fisheries.
Provision of analysis, reporting, and public service announcement on issues concerning oceans, waterways,
and the atmosphere.
Provision of deployable technical expertise in the fields of engineering, earth sciences, oceanography,
meteorology, and fisheries science.
Responsible for preserving and enhancing coastal resources and ecosystem through science-based

Responsible for research and development of environmental products and services.
Responsible for the management and operation of research and surveying assets, e.g., fleets and aircraft.
Responsible for physical science initiatives to increase innovation and industrial competitiveness.
Responsible for establishing education policy, the collection of data on schools, dissemination of research,
and ensuring equal access to education.
Responsible for the synchronization and co-ordination of strategic direction and policy across the

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Acquire Asset

The end-to-end perspective of acquiring an asset, from
initiating and approving the asset request to sourcing and
processing procurement orders and delivering the asset to
the requester.
Request Asset

The act of submitting a request for a new asset.

Approve Request

The act of validating that the asset request meets the

Value Stream Stage Description

Arrange License

The end-to-end perspective of applying for, qualifying for,
and receiving a new or renewal of a license or permit.

Receive
Application

Applicant completes and submits application with supporting
documentation as required for the type of license requested.

Accept Application Determine if the application is complete and ready to be
evaluated, e.g., all required information is present in the
application.
Evaluate
Application

Evaluate the match between the criteria for the specific type
of license criteria and the data on the application.

Issue License

Perform the steps necessary to inform the applicant and
initiate the delivery of the license artifact to the applicant.

Finalize
Application

Complete the recording of the decision for audit trail, inform
other agencies, organizations as appropriate, process fees
associated with the licensing process.

Return to the Value Stream Inventory

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Government Reference Model v5.0

#_x000D_

Description

The end-to-end perspective of planning and executing the means, typically by
ballot, to establish the constituents' choice for, or re-call of, a particular
candidate(s), proposition, plebiscite, or referendum question.
The activities required to conceive, advance, posit, or originate a vote on a
proposition, referendum, and/or election.
The activities required to identify propositions, referendum questions, register
eligible candidates, election representatives and constituents as voters, schedule
voting-related events, identify and deploy resources, book voting venues, address
security concerns, and finalize the plan to conduct a vote.
The activities required to enable the voting to occur, including updating the
electoral register, preparing fiscal analysis of propositions, registering candidates
and election representatives, issuing voting invitation cards, ensuring the safety of
voters and the data integrity of the votes, collecting proxy and postal votes,
monitoring candidate campaigns, advertising polling stations locations, and
The activities required to manage voting and counting operations, including vote
casting, securing, transporting, preparing votes for counting, checking and
recounting as needed, and generally ensuring the integrity of the vote casting and
count.
The activities required to certify the integrity of the voting process, formalize the
outcome, and declare the results.

Copyright Business Architecture Guild 2025

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Create Policy

The end-to-end perspective of creating and updating policies
that govern how the public sector entity will regulate a
constituent organization, or how the public sector entity itself
operates.
Initiate Policy
Request

The initiation of a policy creation or modification as a result of
a request.

Approve Policy
Request

The collection and analysis of research leading to an approval
or denial to proceed with policy formulation.

Formulate Policy

The drafting of a proposed policy or policy modification,
collecting comments, editing, and finalizing the policy to
submit for review.

Approve Policy

The official review and legally binding vote by authorized
persons to establish the creation or modification of a policy.

Publish Policy

The publication of the new or modified policy for
consumption by organizations, institutions, partners, and
other stakeholders.

Return to the Value Stream Inventory

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Decide Legal Case

The end-to-end perspective of bringing a case, evidence, and
testimony through the court system, obtaining a decision,
and enacting the decision.
File Legal Case

According to the customs of the jurisdiction, present a claim
to the right to pursue a legal matter to obtain a resolution.

Prepare for Case
Examination

The activities required by the jurisdiction to prepare for a
formal examination of the evidence of the case.

Conduct Case
Examination

Optional value stream stage in which the activities required
by the jurisdiction to present evidence for a legal case are
conducted.

Determine Case
Outcome

The activities at the end of a formal examination that result in
a decision.

Finalize Legal Case The post-trial activities to record the outcome, expectations,
and next steps, if any.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Deliver Meeting

The end-to-end perspective of planning and executing a
meeting or other interaction.
Initiate Meeting

The act of conceiving, advancing, positing, or originating a
meeting.

Approve Meeting

The act of defining the meeting and its subject matter,
planning the meeting, budgeting and scheduling the
meeting, identifying resources for the meeting, and
approving the meeting.

Prepare Meeting

The act of securing resources, such as people, assets, or
facilities for the meeting.

Conduct Meeting

The act of carrying out the activities defined in the meeting
plan.

Finalize Meeting

The act of concluding the meeting, which may include
activities such as communicating with stakeholders after a
meeting, recording or memorializing the meeting subject
matter, evaluating the outcomes of the meeting, paying for
the meeting, or cleaning up after the meeting.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Deliver Training

The end-to-end perspective of planning, executing, and
communicating a training course (whether in real-time, selfpaced, or on-demand) for the purpose of increasing
knowledge and skills.
Request Training

The act of requesting a unit or curriculum of a training
course.

Define Training
Plan

The act of identifying training course curriculum options to
be delivered to meet the learning, schedule, and budget
objectives, and finalizing a plan to proceed.

Prepare for
Training Delivery

The act of scheduling, making arrangements for, resourcing,
staging, and readying a training course, according to plan, to
prepare for delivery.

Orchestrate
Training Delivery

The act of imparting a training course and validating that it
has been understood.

Finalize PostDelivery Actions

The act of evaluating a training course learning content and
training event delivery metrics and making that information
available to appropriate stakeholders.

Infrastructure

development plans to support those opportunities.

required to meet desired career opportunities.

Resource

Value Stream Stage Description

Develop Strategy

The end-to-end perspective of developing or refining a set
of integrated and aligned visions, goals, objectives, and
courses of action that provide direction and guides activity.

Initiate Strategy
Formulation

The act of commencing a development or refinement of a
strategy based on a given business situation or opportunity.

Scope

strategy through articulation of vision and goals.

Finalize Objectives The act of formulating objectives and associated key
metrics.
Finalize Strategy

The act of validating, finalizing, and disseminating the
strategy, which includes determining courses of action,
related constraints, and desired outcomes.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage

Ensure Policy
Compliance

Description

The end-to-end perspective of ensuring conformance with
legislation and organization-driven policies, from identifying
compliance requirements, implementing controls, evaluating
controls' effectiveness, addressing compliance incidents, and
reporting compliance as required.
Identify Policy Compliance The act of identifying compliance requirements, either through
Requirements
legislation, organizational policy creation, or maintenance.
Define Policy Compliance
Controls

The act of analyzing compliance requirements and identifying
safeguards and controls to be put in place to ensure
compliance.

Implement Policy
Compliance Controls

The act of implementing people, process, and technology
changes and required training to enable the predefined
compliance controls.

Validate Policy Compliance The act of evaluating compliance controls' effectiveness and
Controls
proactively managing compliance incidents, including
disciplinary actions if required.
Report Policy Compliance

The act of reporting compliance to the regulatory bodies and
organization's management.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage

Establish
Agreement

Description

The end-to-end perspective of activities necessary for
establishing a new or updating an existing agreement with a
partner or a constituent.
Receive Request

The act of receiving a request or expressed interest in creating
or updating an agreement and verifying the requester's
identity.

Identify Needs

The act of assessing the needs of the constituent in order to
recommend the agreement.

Collect Approval and
Submission

The act of receiving the requester's approval to proceed as well
as gathering and validating all remaining information needed to
establish or modify an agreement.

Evaluate Risk

The act of both parties, e.g., the requester and the business,
assessing the risk of establishing or updating the agreement
and agreeing to proceed.

Activate Agreement

The act of activating the requester's agreement.

Perform Post-activation The act of performing any post-activation activities, such as
Activities
notifications, compliance verification, or quality assurance
checks.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage

Execute Campaign

Description

The end-to-end perspective of executing a campaign, from
identifying the need for a campaign to planning, designing,
implementing, and measuring the effectiveness of the
campaign.
Request Campaign

The act of submitting a request for a campaign.

Plan Campaign

The act of defining a campaign plan, including campaign targets
and message, delivery channels, implementation schedule,
success criteria, and required campaign budget and resources.

Design Campaign

The act of defining campaign collateral, including target-specific
messaging, graphic designs for each delivery channel.
Implement Campaign The act of delivering campaign content as planned.
Evaluate Campaign

The act of measuring effectiveness of a campaign and identifying
possible optimizations for future execution.

Return to the Value Stream Inventory

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage

Execute Financial
Transaction

Description

The end-to-end perspective involved in completing a financial
transaction for an agreement.
Initiate Transaction

The act of requesting financial activity on an agreement.

Validate Transaction The act of ensuring that the requester has authority to
Request
request the transaction and the agreement is in a valid state
to allow the transaction to occur.
Identify Related
Impacts

The act of identifying all related effects of the transaction,
including, for example, fees and charges.

Perform Transaction The act of applying request changes to the agreement
balance and calculating the new agreement balance.
Notify Stakeholders

The act of notifying all stakeholders of the transaction and
related events.

Verify Compliance

The act of ensuring that processed transactions are recorded
and retained in accordance with organization and regulatory
policy.

Value Stream Stage Description

Obtain
Accreditation

The end-to-end perspective of applying for, qualifying for,
and receiving a new or renewal of a certification.

Receive
Application

Applicant completes and submits application with supporting
documentation as required for the type of accreditation
requested.

Accept Application Determine if the application is complete and ready to be
evaluated, e.g., all required information is present in the
application.
Evaluate
Application

Evaluate the match between the criteria for the specific type
of accreditation criteria and the data on the application.

Issue License

Perform the steps necessary to inform the applicant and
initiate the delivery of the certification artifact to the
applicant.

Finalize
Application

Complete the recording of the decision for audit trail, inform
other agencies, organizations as appropriate, process fees
associated with the accreditation process.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Obtain Financial
Assistance

The end-to-end perspective of a government organization
receiving a request for, approving, and providing financial
assistance.

Submit Request

An external party identifies a need for assistance, investigates
options, creates a request for assistance, and submits the
request to the government organization.

Approve Request

The government organization receives and reviews the
request and decides whether to approve.

Establish
Agreement

The organization works with stakeholders to establish and
approve both the agreement and its delivery plan.

Deliver Assistance Financial assistance is delivered to the requester as per the
agreement and plan.
Appraise Service

A review is conducted of the financial assistance, covering the
design of the service, its delivery, and the outcomes are
delivered for the constituent.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Obtain Government
Service

The end-to-end perspective of submitting a request, being
qualified for, and receiving the requested service.
Submit Request

Applicant or their proxy completes and submits application with
supporting documentation as required for the type of
government service requested.

Accept Request

Determine whether all required information is present in the
application, evaluate the match between the criteria for the
specific type of government service and the applicant's
qualifications as represented in the application data.

Establish
Agreement

Establish and approve the service agreement and its delivery plan,
complete the recording of the decision for audit trail, inform other
agencies and organizations as appropriate, process fees
associated with transaction processing.
The act of providing the approved government service to the
constituent using a delivery method most appropriate for the type
of service and the requester's circumstances.

Deliver
Government
Service
Appraise Service

A review is conducted of the government service, covering the
design of the service, its delivery, and the outcomes delivered for
the constituent.

The end-to-end perspective of establishing the right to own,

privately-owned land.

of the land.

Demarcate
location on authoritative maps.
Geographic Space

arrive at an agreement of ownership of land rights.

Finalize Decision

The activities of review and disposition of the proposal by
appropriate decision-making authority, communicating the
decision, making payments, registering and publishing the
land rights in the official record of the jurisdiction.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Onboard Human
Resource

The end-to-end perspective of identifying, exploring, and
selecting an individual to fill a need within an organization.
Request Position

The act of submitting a recruitment requisition for a vacancy
required to perform work for the organization.

Validate Position

The act of verifying that the recruitment requisition's financial
and business justification criteria are acceptable.

Source Individuals The act of finding individuals who may qualify for the open
position and validating their interest.
Evaluate
Individuals

The act of assessing the potential candidates against the
open position requirements and extending an offer to the
most qualified individual.

Finalize
Acceptance

The act of negotiating the employment agreement terms and
conditions.

Onboard
Individual

The act of bringing an individual into the organization and
providing necessary training and resources for them to
effectively start contributing.

Return to the Value Stream Inventory

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Onboard Partner

The end-to-end perspective of identifying and commencing
business with other organizations for mutual benefit.

Identify Need

The act of defining the business requirements for goods and
services that cannot be obtained internally.

Vet Potential
Partner

The act of validating that the potential partner is capable of
delivering on the value proposition and meets ethical
guidelines.

Negotiate Terms

The act of reviewing and negotiating the terms of the
contract including such things as cost, scope, and length of
engagement.

Formalize
Agreement

The act of reaching final agreement on the terms of the
contract.

Induct Partner

The act of onboarding the partner to make them familiar with
how they are expected to engage with the organization.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Optimize Reserves

The end-to-end perspective of establishing a stated amount or
percent of liquid assets that the government estimates as
needed on hand for unearned premium reserves and
outstanding losses, such as claims and related outstanding
liabilities.
Create Reserves
Forecast

The action of making assumptions about future financial
trends using techniques such as analysis of historical data,
benchmarking, and budgetary planning.

Analyze Risks

The act of defining and evaluating the uncertainty concerning
the possibility of loss to the organization.

Determine Risk
Exposure

The act of quantifying a potential loss to the organization.

Establish Target
Levels

The act of determining the required levels of reserves that will
keep the organization financially able to meet its obligations
and liabilities.

Notify
Stakeholders

The act of completing activities that will inform the
stakeholders of the organization's plan for reserve
management.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Pass Legislation

The end-to-end perspective of drafting a bill, consideration and
revision, and approval of the legislation, enactment into law,
and possible nullification of outdated laws.
Initiate Legislation Act of proposing and beginning the effort to pass legislation.
Draft Legislation

Act of drafting the initially proposed legislation.

Approve
Legislation

Act of holding hearings, passing through multiple committee,
legislative bodies, reconciliations, and achieving final vote to be
signed.

Sign Legislation

Act of formally signing legislation into law, typically by an
executive body.

Enact Legislation

Act of preparing for and having the legislation go into effect.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage

Register/Grant Intellectual
Property Rights

Description

The end-to-end perspective of requesting a patent,
trademark, or copyright, reviewing the request, and
granting the request.

Initiate Intellectual
Act of submitting an application to register or grant
Property Rights Request rights.
Accept Request

Act of accepting an application as valid.

Grant Preliminary
Request

Act of preliminarily registering or granting of rights,
pending public review.

Clear Public Review
Period

Act of opening up a registration or granting request for
public review and review period expiring without a
challenge.

Register/Grant
Intellectual Property
Rights

Act of formally granting or registering intellectual
property and notifying all stakeholders.

Resolve Incident

The end-to-end perspective of activities necessary to identify,
scope, track, and address an incident as well as identify areas of
improvement in order to reduce future likelihood or improve
future responses.
Recognize Incident

The act of identifying and acknowledging an incident.

Determine Cause
and Impact

The act of classifying and investigating the incident to determine
the root cause and impact.

Formulate Response The act of formulating a course of action to correct or offset the
effects of the incident.
Conclude Incident

The act of applying the determined course of action to resolve,
correct or offset the effects of the incident.

Identify
Improvements

The act of deciding on changes to products and/or operational
processes to prevent or reduce future recurrence or improve
future resolution.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Settle Migration

The end-to-end perspective of requesting, qualifying for, and
receiving authorization for immigration or emigration.

Receive Migration
Request

Applicant completes and submits a migration request, using
available channels, with supporting documentation as required
for the type of immigration product requested, and completing
payment for any required product/service fees.

Accept Request for The activities required to perform a detailed assessment of the
Migration
application, verify and validate the information and supporting
documentation provided, and confirm the applicant's identity.
Decide Migration
Request Outcome

The activities required to evaluate the request against eligibility,
suitability, entitlement, and threat criteria, interview the migrant
applicant where necessary, liaise and communicate with
stakeholders as required, arrive at a decision and complete the
recording of the decision for case history.

Finalize Migration
Request Outcome

The activities required to produce and complete any required
documentation and artifacts relating to the migration
determination, deliver the service to the migrant, and
communicate the outcome to other agencies and stakeholders.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Settle Payment
Obligation

The end-to-end set of activities necessary for determining,
communicating, and settling (exchanging funds against) a
payment obligation.
Initiate Payment

The act of initiating a payment obligation.

Determine
Payment
Obligation

The act of gathering and validating all information necessary
and calculating and defining a payment obligation.

Communicate
Payment
Obligation

The act of formulating and communicating the payment
obligation to the appropriate stakeholder(s).

Validate Payment The act of reconciling and validating the legitimacy and
Obligation
accuracy of the payment obligation.
Exchange Funds

The act of transferring funds against the payment obligation.

Update Financial
Records

The act of recording the exchange of funds in financial
accounts and updating the status of the payment obligation.

Value Stream

Value Stream Stage Description

Trade Financial
Instrument

The end-to-end perspective of executing a financial
instrument trade, including clearing and settlement.
Initiate Trade

The act of making a request for trading a financial
instrument.

Select Accredited
Broker-Dealer

The act of determining and selecting which broker-dealer will
execute the financial instrument trade.

Validate Trade
Request

The act of verifying if the requested financial instrument is
suitable for the investor according to established investment
goals.

Obtain Trade
Quotes

The act of obtaining all available quotes for the requested
instrument exchange.

Execute Trade
Order

The act of fulfilling, i.e., entering into an agreement with the
counterparty to exchange the instrument, the trade order
externally and matching to the investment trade agreements.
The act of exchanging the agreed-upon financial instruments
and verifying that the trade was done in accordance with all
policies, regulations, and procedures.

Settle Trade

Government Reference Model v5.0 Change Log
Change
Level 2 pattern definition has been improved and applied consistently to the Level 1 and Level 2 objects that use the pattern,
"Ability to establish and identify a <business object>."
Level 2 pattern definition has been improved and applied consistently to the Level 1 and Level 2 objects that use the pattern,
"Ability to recognize a <business object>."
Where a Level 1 or Level 2 object was matched to "Meeting", the matching is now to "Interaction"
Level 2 pattern definition has been improved and applied consistently to the Level 1 and Level 2 objects that use the pattern,
"Ability to define, interpret, and enforce the right to view, use, or modify a <business object> or its component parts."
Access Constraints Definition pattern is, "Ability to determine access rights limitations for a <business object>."
Access Enforcement pattern is, "Ability to impose access rights limitations for a <business object>."
Level 2 pattern definition has been improved and applied consistently to the Level 1 and Level 2 objects that use the pattern,
"Ability to determine how well a <business object> is meeting specification and objective levels, or delivering against plan."
Definition updated to "Ability to determine acceptable or unacceptable levels of performance for a <business object>."
Definition updated to "Ability to determine acceptable or unacceptable levels of performance for a <business object>."
L2 pattern has been split into separate L2 Authentication Management and L2 Authorization Management capabilities
Level 2 pattern definition has been improved and applied consistently to the Level 1 and Level 2objects that use the pattern, "Ability
to identify, assess, aggregate, articulate, and incorporate various exposures to harm, danger, or loss associated with a <business
object>."
Definition updated to "Ability to identify and define the level of risk associated with a <business object>."
"Ability to identify and define the level of acceptable risk associated with a <business object>."
"Ability to consider a collective set of risk factors about a <business object> and represent them from a rationalized perspective."

<business object>."

New L1: Schedule Management has been promoted to a level 1 capability, no longer as a level 2 under Work Management. It has
also been elaborated to include information management, access management, risk management, and performance management
using the standard patterns for these. Schedule Validation and Schedule Structuring have been added as level 2 capabilities. The
level 1 definition has been improved. A new set of capabilities related to Schedule Element have been added: i.e., Definition,
Information Management, and Matching.

"Standard Conformance Measurement".

Submission Management has been promoted to a level 1 capability, no longer as a level 2 under Work Management. The definition
has been improved, as well as the definition of several lower level capabilities (i.e., Submission Facilitation, Submission
Interpretation, Submission Routing, and Submission Acknowledgement). It has also been elaborated to include risk management
and performance management using the standard patterns for these.
